  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8fbbf1f9-3b46-4524-bd4f-793f6e36a163'
      });

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer13737236099480788052"> The only Finnish novel adopted into a Hollywood film <p>Mika Waltari's 1945 novel The Egyptian was turned into a DeLuxe Color epic film by 20th Century Fox in 1954 and was nominated for an academy award a year later.</p> A 1940s #1 Bestseller and a Historic Novel All-Time Favorite <p>A historic novel all-time favorite, after its translation in English from Swedish, The Egyptian top</p></span>
  <span id="freeText13737236099480788052" style="display:none"> The only Finnish novel adopted into a Hollywood film <p>Mika Waltari's 1945 novel The Egyptian was turned into a DeLuxe Color epic film by 20th Century Fox in 1954 and was nominated for an academy award a year later.</p> A 1940s #1 Bestseller and a Historic Novel All-Time Favorite <p>A historic novel all-time favorite, after its translation in English from Swedish, The Egyptian topped the bestseller charts in 1949 and the years following. </p><p>The protagonist of the novel is the fictional character Sinuhe, the royal physician, who tells the story in exile after Akhenaten's fall and death. Apart from incidents in Egypt, the novel charts Sinuhe's travels in then Egyptian-dominated Syria, in Mitanni, Babylon, Minoan Crete, Mitanni, and among the Hittites.</p><p>The main character of the novel is named after a character in an ancient Egyptian text commonly known as The Story of Sinuhe. The original story dates to a time long before that of Akhenaten: texts are known from as early as the 12th Dynasty.</p><p>Much concerned about the historical accuracy of his detailed description of ancient Egyptian life forced the author to carry out considerable research into the subject. The result has been praised not only by readers but also by Egyptologists.</p><p>Waltari had long been interested in Akhenaten and wrote a play about him which was staged in Helsinki in 1938. World War II provided the final impulse for exploring the subject in a novel which, although depicting events that took place over 3,300 years ago</p><p> </p></span>
  <a data-text-id="13737236099480788052" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4109736797303710958"><b>The Egyptian (Sinuhe egyptiläinen), Mika Waltari</b><br/><br/>The Egyptian is a historical novel by Mika Waltari. It was first published in Finnish in 1945, and in an abridged English translation by Naomi Walford in 1949, apparently from Swedish rather than Finnish. So far, it is the only Finnish novel to be adapted into a Hollywood film, which it was, in 1954. <br/><br/>The Egyptian is the first and the most successful, of Waltari's great historical novels. It is set in Ancient Egypt, mostly during the reign of Pharao</span>
  <span id="freeText4109736797303710958" style="display:none"><b>The Egyptian (Sinuhe egyptiläinen), Mika Waltari</b><br /><br />The Egyptian is a historical novel by Mika Waltari. It was first published in Finnish in 1945, and in an abridged English translation by Naomi Walford in 1949, apparently from Swedish rather than Finnish. So far, it is the only Finnish novel to be adapted into a Hollywood film, which it was, in 1954. <br /><br />The Egyptian is the first and the most successful, of Waltari's great historical novels. It is set in Ancient Egypt, mostly during the reign of Pharaoh Akhenaten of the 18th Dynasty, whom some have claimed to be the first monotheistic ruler in the world.<br /><br />عنوانها: «سینوحه»؛ «سینوهه»؛ «سینوهه پزشک مخصوص فرعون»؛ «سینوهه کاهن اعظم مصر»؛ «سینوهه مصری»؛ تاریخ نخستین خوانش ماه اکتبر سال 1998میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: سینوهه پزشک مخصوص فرعون؛ نویسنده: میکا ولتاری؛ مترجم و مولف: ذبیح الله منصوری؛ تهران، زرین، 1366؛ در دو جلد؛ چاپ پنجاه و هشتم 1387؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان فنلاندی - سده 20م<br /><br />عنوان: سینوحه؛ نویسنده: میکا والتاری؛ مترجم: احمد بهپور؛ تهران، نشر رضا، 1369، در 642ص؛ چاپ دیگر تهران، جویا، 1370، در 642ص؛ چاپ چهارم 1377؛ پنجم 1379؛ ششم 1381؛ هشتم 1385؛ نهم 1386؛ چاپ دیگر تهران، جویا - آسیم، چاپ دهم 1388؛ در 642ص؛ شابک 9789646092187؛ چاپ دوازدهم 1395؛ در دو جلد؛ شابک دوره 9789642895878؛ جلد یک 9789642895847؛ جلد دو 9789642895854؛ <br /><br />مترجمهای دیگری نیز خانمها و آقایان: «احمدسادات عقیلی»؛ «محسن باطنی»؛ «داوود نعمت اللهی»؛ «مرتضی اسدخواه»؛ «ابراهیم صفریان»؛ «عزیزعلی امیری‌زاده»؛ «سعیده هاشمی»؛ «امیر رمزی»؛ «فرشته کریمی»؛ «امیرعباس طبا»؛ «ابراهیم صفریان»؛ «هاله هنرزاد»؛ «رضا زارع»، «زهره زندیه»؛ این اثر را ترجمه کرده اند، نوشته هایم را در باره ی مشخصات کتابهای ترجمه شده از این اثر توسط نامبردگان بالا را که به دشواری یافته بودم نیز به ناروا پاک کرده اند<br /><br />سینوهه نام رمانی تاریخی به قلم «میکا والتاری»، نویسنده «فنلاندی» است، که بر اساس رخدادهای دوران فرعون «آخناتون» نوشته شده است؛ فیلمی هالیوودی نیز بر اساس همین کتاب در سال 1954میلادی ساخته شده است سبک روانشاد «ذبیح‌ الله منصوری» ترجمه-تألیف بوده؛ در مقدمه ی دکتر «احمد بهپور» می‌خوانیم: در مورد این که «سینوهه» شخصیتی است واقعی، یا افسانه‌ ای، چیزی دانسته نشد، شاید او نیز همانند «یل سیستان» باشد؛ که «فردوسی» بزرگ از ایشان «رستم دستان» را ساخته است….؛ جناب محسن باطنی به دلیل آشنایی با ریشه‌ های زبانهای اسپانیایی و ایتالیایی، انگلیسی و ترکی استانبولی، برای ترجمه کتاب «سینوهه»، به پژوهش جامعی پرداخته، و متن بسیار کامل و روانی را با ترجمه ی همزمان از هر دو نسخه انگلیسی و اسپانیایی، ارائه داده اند؛ همچنین تصاویری جذاب از متن و نسخه اصلی همین کتاب، که به زبان «هیروگلیف» است، در متن ترجمه ی کتاب آورده اند؛ <br /><br />داستان دربارهٔ شخصیتی است، که در هنگام تولد، او را در یک سبد دستباف بگذاشته، و به رود نیل سپرده‌ بودند؛ و خانواده‌ ای ناداری او را یافته، و به فرزندی بزرگ می‌کنند؛ «سینوهه» در ادامه، به مقام کاهنی و پزشکی (مخصوصِ فرعون) می‌رسند، و سفرهایی را به «بابل»، «سوریه»، و کناره دریای مدیترانه می‌کنند؛ در طول آن سفر، با رخدادهای گوناگون روبرو می‌شوند؛ در میانه‌ های داستان، ایشان به هویت راستین پدر و مادرش پی می‌برند؛ یکی از ویژگی‌های بارز این کتاب، توصیف نحوه ی زندگی و اوضاع اجتماعی کشورهای «مصر»، «سوریه»، «بابل»، «هیتی»، و «میتانی»، در دوران «آخناتون» است؛ که در میان سال‌های 1351پیش از میلاد تا سال 1334پیش از زادروز حضرت مسیح می‌زیسته است<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 17/08/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_63136493" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/63136493" />
    <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani"><img alt="Ahmad Sharabiani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194930432p2/614778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/63136493?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmad Sharabiani" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani">Ahmad Sharabiani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/6046605">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=novels">novels</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63136493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11467046658752683319">The Egyptian (Sinuhe egyptiläinen #1–2), Mika Waltari<br/>The Egyptian is a historical novel by Mika Waltari. It was first published in Finnish in 1945, and in an abridged English translation by Naomi Walford in 1949, apparently from Swedish rather than Finnish. So far, it is the only Finnish novel to be adapted into a Hollywood film, which it was, in 1954. The Egyptian is the first and the most successful, of Waltari's great historical novels. It is set in Ancient Egypt, mostly during the reign of P</span>
  <span id="freeText11467046658752683319" style="display:none">The Egyptian (Sinuhe egyptiläinen #1–2), Mika Waltari<br />The Egyptian is a historical novel by Mika Waltari. It was first published in Finnish in 1945, and in an abridged English translation by Naomi Walford in 1949, apparently from Swedish rather than Finnish. So far, it is the only Finnish novel to be adapted into a Hollywood film, which it was, in 1954. The Egyptian is the first and the most successful, of Waltari's great historical novels. It is set in Ancient Egypt, mostly during the reign of Pharaoh Akhenaten of the 18th Dynasty, whom some have claimed to be the first monotheistic ruler in the world.<br /><br />عنوانها: سینوحه؛ سینوهه؛ سینوهه پزشک مخصوص فرعون؛ سینوهه کاهن اعظم مصر؛ سینوهه مصری؛ تاریخ نخستین خوانش: در ماه اکتبر سال 1998 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: سینوهه پزشک مخصوص فرعون، جلد دوم؛ نویسنده: میکا ولتاری؛ مترجم و مولف: ذبیح الله منصوری؛ تهران، زرین، 1366؛ در دو جلد؛ چاپ پنجاه و هشتم 1387؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان فنلاندی - سده 20 م<br /><br />سینوهه، عنوان رمانی تاریخی، به قلم: «میکا والتاری»، نویسنده ی فنلاندی ست، که براساس رخدادهای دوران فرعون: «آخناتون»، نوشته شده است. فیلمی هالیوودی نیز، براساس همین کتاب، در سال 1954 میلادی ساخته شده است. کتاب در ایران، توسط جنابان آقایان: ذبیح‌ الله منصوری، احمد بهپور، احمدسادات عقیلی، و محسن باطنی، به فارسی ترجمه شده است، گرچه سبک روانشاد ذبیح‌ الله منصوری ترجمه-تألیف بوده است. در مقدمه ی جناب دکتر احمد بهپور می‌خوانیم: «در مورد اینکه سینوهه شخصیتی است واقعی، یا افسانه‌ ای، چیزی دانسته نشد، شاید او نیز همانند: یل سیستان باشد؛ که فردوسی بزرگ، از ایشان: رستم دستان را ساخته است»….؛ جناب آقای محسن باطنی، به دلیل آشنایی با ریشه‌ های زبانهای: اسپانیایی، ایتالیایی، انگلیسی، و ترکی استانبولی، برای ترجمه ی کتاب سینوهه، به پژوهش جامعی پرداخته، و متن بسیار کامل، و روانی را با ترجمه ی همزمان، از هر دو نسخه ی انگلیسی، و اسپانیایی، ارائه داده است. همچنین تصاویری جذاب از متن، و نسخه اصلی همین کتاب، که به زبان هیروگلیف است، در متن ترجمه ی کتاب آورده است. داستان، درباره ی شخصیتی است، که در هنگام تولد، او را در یک سبد دستباف گذاشته، و به رود نیل سپرده‌ اند؛ و خانواده‌ ای فقیر، او را یافته، و به فرزندی بزرگ می‌کنند. سینوهه در ادامه، به مقام کاهنی، و پزشکی (پزشک ویژه ی فرعون) می‌رسد، و سفرهایی را به: بابل، سوریه، و کناره ی دریای مدیترانه، می‌کند. در طول سفر، با رخدادهای گوناگون، روبرو می‌شود. در میانه‌ های داستان، او به هویت راستین پدر و مادرش، پی می‌برد. یکی از ویژگی‌های بارز این کتاب، توصیف نحوه ی زندگی، و اوضاع اجتماعی کشورهای: مصر، سوریه، بابل، هیتی، میتانی، در دوران آخناتون است؛ که در میان سال‌های 1351 تا سال 1334 پیش از زادروز حضرت مسیح، می‌زیسته است. ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="11467046658752683319" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17196088042391299891">Sinuhe egyptiläinen = Sinuhe der Agypter‬ = Sinuhe the Egyptian, Mika Waltari <br/>The Egyptian (Sinuhe egyptiläinen, Sinuhe the Egyptian) is a historical novel by Mika Waltari. It was first published in Finnish in 1945, and in an abridged English translation by Naomi Walford in 1949, apparently from Swedish rather than Finnish. So far, it is the only Finnish novel to be adapted into a Hollywood film, which it was, in 1954. The protagonist of the novel is the fictional character Sinuhe, the royal phy</span>
  <span id="freeText17196088042391299891" style="display:none">Sinuhe egyptiläinen = Sinuhe der Agypter‬ = Sinuhe the Egyptian, Mika Waltari <br />The Egyptian (Sinuhe egyptiläinen, Sinuhe the Egyptian) is a historical novel by Mika Waltari. It was first published in Finnish in 1945, and in an abridged English translation by Naomi Walford in 1949, apparently from Swedish rather than Finnish. So far, it is the only Finnish novel to be adapted into a Hollywood film, which it was, in 1954. The protagonist of the novel is the fictional character Sinuhe, the royal physician, who tells the story in exile after Akhenaten's fall and death. Apart from incidents in Egypt, the novel charts Sinuhe's travels in then Egyptian-dominated Syria (Levant), in Mitanni, Babylon, Minoan Crete, and among the Hittites. ...<br />عنوانها: سینوحه؛ سینوهه؛ سینوهه پزشک مخصوص فرعون؛ سینوهه کاهن اعظم مصر؛ سینوهه مصری؛ نویسنده: میکا والتاری؛ تاریخ نخستین خوانش: ماه اکتبر سال 1998 میلادی<br />عنوان: سینوحه؛ نویسنده: میکا والتاری؛ مترجم: احمد بهپور؛ تهران، نشر رضا، 1369، در 642 ص؛ چاپ دیگر: تهران، جویا، 1370، در 642 ص؛ چاپ چهارم 1377؛ پنجم 1379؛ ششم 1381؛ هشتم 1385؛ نهم 1386؛ چاپ دیگر: تهران، جویا - آسیم، چاپ دهم 1388؛ در 642 ص؛ شابک: 9789646092187؛ چاپ دوازدهم 1395؛ در دو جلد؛ شابک دوره: 9789642895878؛ جلد یک: 9789642895847؛ جلد دو: 9789642895854؛ موضوع: داستانهای تاریخس از نویسندگان فنلاندی - قرن 20 م<br />عنوان: سینوهه پزشک مخصوص فرعون، در دو جلد؛ نویسنده: میکا والتاری؛ مترجم: ذبیح الله منصوری؛ تهران، زرین، چاپ هشتم 1366؛ در دو جلد 629 ص؛ چاپ پنجاه و هشتم 1387؛ <br />مترجمهای دیگری نیز این اثر را ترجمه کرده اند؛ <br />داستان درباره ی شخصیتی ست که در هنگام تولد او را در یک سبد دستباف بگذاشته و به رود نیل سپرده‌ اند و خانواده‌ ای فقیر او را یافته و به فرزندی بزرگ می‌کنند. سینوهه در ادامه به مقام کاهنی و پزشکی (مخصوصِ فرعون) می‌رسد و سفرهایی را به بابل و سوریه و کناره دریای مدیترانه می‌کند. در طول این سفر با رخدادهای گوناگون روبرو می‌شود. در بازگشت به مصر برای نجات مصر، از حرفه ی پزشکی خویش سود می‌برد. در میانه‌ های داستان او به هویت راستین پدر و مادرش پی می‌برد. یکی از ویژگی‌های بارز این داستان، توصیف دقیق نحوه ی زندگی مردمان و اوضاع اجتماعی کشورهای مصر، سوریه، بابل، هیتی، میتانی در دوران آخناتون است؛ که در میان سال‌های 1334–1351 پیش از زادروز مسیح می‌زیسته است. این کتاب را نامدارانی همچون: ذبیح‌ الله منصوری، دکتر احمد بهپور، احمدسادات عقیلی و محسن باطنی و دیگران از نامداران ترجمه به فارسی برگردانده اند. ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="17196088042391299891" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1055558744" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1055558744" />
    <a title="Kaśyap" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8660547-ka-yap"><img alt="Kaśyap" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605598480p2/8660547.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1055558744?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaśyap" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaśyap" href="/user/show/8660547-ka-yap">Kaśyap</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781556524417" href="/book/show/59282.The_Egyptian">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8660547-ka-yap?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8660547-ka-yap?shelf=historical">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1055558744" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18117551049019795">A remarkable historical novel set in ancient Egypt mainly during the reign of the pharaoh Akhenaton, who tried to bring monotheistic worship of Aton to Egypt. His reign was marked by internal conflict and he and his descendants in the 18th dynasty were later denounced by Horemheb, and their names were erased in the Egyptian records. The worship of Aton is speculated to be a precursor of Judaism.<br/><br/>The book is in the form of autobiography of Sinuhe a physician who rises to become an advisor and frie</span>
  <span id="freeText18117551049019795" style="display:none">A remarkable historical novel set in ancient Egypt mainly during the reign of the pharaoh Akhenaton, who tried to bring monotheistic worship of Aton to Egypt. His reign was marked by internal conflict and he and his descendants in the 18th dynasty were later denounced by Horemheb, and their names were erased in the Egyptian records. The worship of Aton is speculated to be a precursor of Judaism.<br /><br />The book is in the form of autobiography of Sinuhe a physician who rises to become an advisor and friend of pharaohs and kings. His travels take him from Egypt to Syria, Babylon, Mitanni, Hattusa and Crete at the end of Minoan civilization. Albeit set in the 14th century Egypt, the travels of Sinuhe paint a timeless human story in all its foibles and follies. It reveals the brutal reality of human civilization where ultimately the strong oppress the weak and it is the poor who always suffer.<br /><br />Akhenaton is portrayed as a utopian dreamer and visionary who is completely out of touch with the reality. All his best intentions lead to death and disaster. Sinuhe isn’t exactly a very likable character. He often comes off as cowardly, self-centred and arrogant, but also as one who tries to do good but only at the price of losing everything.<br /><br />The novel is thoroughly researched and historically accurate for its time. There are some inaccuracies, like Tutankhamen was the son of Akhenaton and Rameses was not the son of Horemheb, but I’m guessing these weren’t known at the time the book was written.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18117551049019795" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12606922662167438606">This must be my 5th go'round on this book, I re-read it every so often, because I really do consider it to be a classic. <br/>It was considered almost obscene in it's day, because of the subject matters that were delt with.   <span id="freeText12606922662167438606" style="display:none">This must be my 5th go'round on this book, I re-read it every so often, because I really do consider it to be a classic. <br />It was considered almost obscene in it's day, because of the subject matters that were delt with. But it is rather tame for today. I first read it and found it quite shocking many years ago, but I have a fascination with Egyptian history and I just could not put it down.<br />I was made into a movie sometime in the 50's or 60's I belive and many things were glossed over but it still was pretty racey. <br />The epic tale is filled with the grandure of ancient Egypt and the carnal life that was prevalent at the tome of the Pharoahs, so it really exposes some of the rawness of the worse of human nature, and obsession.<br />But it also deals with intense love and forgiveness, in somecases undeserved. <br />A very powerful look into the best and the ABSOLUTE worst behavior, and morals of a decaying society that once ruled the entire world! </span>

<div id="review_710892637" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/710892637" />
    <a title="Lisa (Harmonybites)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2596042-lisa-harmonybites"><img alt="Lisa (Harmonybites)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1337396485p2/2596042.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/710892637?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa (Harmonybites)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa (Harmonybites)" href="/user/show/2596042-lisa-harmonybites">Lisa (Harmonybites)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781556524417" href="/book/show/59282.The_Egyptian">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Historical Fiction</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2596042-lisa-harmonybites?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2596042-lisa-harmonybites?shelf=2013-around-the-world">2013-around-the-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2596042-lisa-harmonybites?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2596042-lisa-harmonybites?shelf=novels">novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2596042-lisa-harmonybites?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer710892637" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5661126977161824804">This just misses five stars--because it took me a long time to warm up to the Sinuhe, the protagonist and narrator, and it's just a little bit too much of a downer. So no, I wouldn't call this a happy tale--but it is a rich epic and great historical fiction of Ancient Egypt under Akhenaton, its heretic pharaoh. Had I not known going in, I wouldn't have guessed this novel was written in 1945. Although that might explain some of its bleakness--I've read that when it was published, it resonated wit</span>
  <span id="freeText5661126977161824804" style="display:none">This just misses five stars--because it took me a long time to warm up to the Sinuhe, the protagonist and narrator, and it's just a little bit too much of a downer. So no, I wouldn't call this a happy tale--but it is a rich epic and great historical fiction of Ancient Egypt under Akhenaton, its heretic pharaoh. Had I not known going in, I wouldn't have guessed this novel was written in 1945. Although that might explain some of its bleakness--I've read that when it was published, it resonated with people who had seen humanistic ideals collapse in the face of Stalin, Hitler, the Holocaust. <br /><br />This is set in Ancient Egypt over 1,300 years before the birth of Christ. Akhenation is thought to be the first monotheist, so he holds some fascination for Jews, Christians and Muslims. Before this I had read Naguib Mahfouz's <i>Akhenaten, Dweller in Truth</i>. Mahfouz is a Muslim and I thought I could detect that coloring his novel. Waltari, for his part, was supposedly a believing Christian. His novel doesn't come across as Christian fiction though--at all. As I said, it doesn't come across as written in 1945. I didn't feel as if there was a overlay of a worldview alien to the time in which this was set--and for me that's the mark of great historical fiction, that you feel transported to another place and time, rather than reading modern people in historical costumes. In fact, I think Waltari did almost too well--as I said it took a long time for me to warm to Sinuhe. Especially in his youth he was arrogant, misogynist, and too-stupid-to-live. But there are positive, strong female characters in this novel--they're just not very apparent early on. <br /><br />And Waltari set this not just in Egypt--this is like a grand tour of the Bronze Age world--Egypt, Canaan, Syria, Babylon, Hatti, Crete. There are allusions to both Biblical stories and Greek myth. Sinuhe was found as a baby floating in the river on a reed boat and Minea, one of the positive female characters, is a bull-leaper from Minoan Crete--and there is a minotaur and a labyrinth. According to what I gather from online, Waltari did extensive research for this book and garnered praise even from Egyptologists. So truly, this novel is a great ride I'd recommend to anyone looking for great historical fiction--even if I found it a rather melancholy read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5661126977161824804" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It's long and dense and requires a little effort to read, but because it's longer, you feel more involved with the main character. The story is about a really interesting era in Egyptian history that most don't focus on, and I think I learned quite a lot from it. I am interested in Mika's other books now...</span>

<div id="review_2871919451" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2871919451" />
    <a title="Tamara Agha-Jaffar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51003559-tamara-agha-jaffar"><img alt="Tamara Agha-Jaffar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452453836p2/51003559.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2871919451?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tamara Agha-Jaffar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tamara Agha-Jaffar" href="/user/show/51003559-tamara-agha-jaffar">Tamara Agha-Jaffar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781556524417" href="/book/show/59282.The_Egyptian">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51003559-tamara-agha-jaffar?shelf=2019-reading-challenge">2019-reading-challenge</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51003559-tamara-agha-jaffar?shelf=middle-east-and-africa">middle-east-and-africa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51003559-tamara-agha-jaffar?shelf=classics">classics</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2871919451" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4586468342870572764"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/59282.The_Egyptian' title='The Egyptian by Mika Waltari' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Egyptian</a> by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/33472.Mika_Waltari' title='Mika Waltari' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mika Waltari</a>, translated by Naomi Walford, was an international best seller in the 1940s. The novel immerses the reader in the life and times of ancient Egypt during the reign of the rebel pharaoh Akhnaton. The story unfolds in the first-person narrative of Sinuhe, the personal physician to Akhnaton.<br/><br/>Born under mysterious circumstances, Sinuhe is adopted by a couple who shower him with love and support. His success as a student enables him to work his way up through the many layer</span>
  <span id="freeText4586468342870572764" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/59282.The_Egyptian" title="The Egyptian by Mika Waltari" rel="nofollow noopener">The Egyptian</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/33472.Mika_Waltari" title="Mika Waltari" rel="nofollow noopener">Mika Waltari</a>, translated by Naomi Walford, was an international best seller in the 1940s. The novel immerses the reader in the life and times of ancient Egypt during the reign of the rebel pharaoh Akhnaton. The story unfolds in the first-person narrative of Sinuhe, the personal physician to Akhnaton.<br /><br />Born under mysterious circumstances, Sinuhe is adopted by a couple who shower him with love and support. His success as a student enables him to work his way up through the many layers of hierarchy until he becomes the personal physician to the pharaoh. As an intimate of the court and one who is privy to its secrets, he describes in vivid detail the palace intrigues, sexual liaisons, marriages, murders, and shifting political alliances. <br /><br />At times, self-absorbed, arrogant, and cowardly; at times, heroic and generous, Sinuhe emerges as a conflicted soul, gravitating from one extreme to the other. He shows compassion by healing the poor and needy without demanding compensation. But when embroiled in palace politics, he commits murder and inflicts brutal revenge on his enemies. On the one hand, he sympathizes with and tries to propagate Akhnaton’s vision of the equality of all human beings under the one god; on the other hand, he is convinced of Akhnaton’s madness and responsibility for the breakdown of law and order in Egypt and its surrounding empire.<br /><br />Waltari demonstrates his consummate skill as a writer by creating a compelling texture of ancient Egypt. His research is impressive. Egypt comes alive with its hustle and bustle, pungent odors, opulence, intense heat, noisy streets, graphic violence, wars, exploitation, territorial skirmishes, extremes in poverty and wealth, systemic brutality and oppression, rituals and mythology. Waltari’s re-creation of Crete with its bull dancers and of Babylon in all its ancient splendor are particularly memorable. Sinuhe’s diction sounds old world appropriate and sustains reader interest with its intricate, vivid details. There are many noteworthy phrases peppering the novel, one of which is the amusing reference to a birth in poverty as a birth “with dung between your toes.”<br /><br />The characters are well-developed and believable. Their behavior is self-serving; their morality questionable. Some forge friendships with Sinuhe. Perhaps the most delightful relationship is that of Sinuhe with his one-eyed, self-aggrandizing slave, Kaptah. Kaptah’s droll comments, antics, and down-to-earth perspective ingratiate their way into Sinuhe’s heart until Sinuhe grants him his freedom and trusts him to manage his worldly assets. Kaptah proves to be loyal to his former master as well as an astute business man. He freely confesses to stealing from Sinuhe only what amounts to a reasonable amount. Their relationship endures, blossoming into a charming friendship of opposites.<br /><br />The novel is rich in historical details, presenting a panoramic but bleak view of ancient Egypt during the time of Pharaoh Akhnaton. It brings to life a turbulent time in Egypt’s history, a time plagued with political intrigue and internal conflicts because a pharaoh defied an institutionalized belief system with its powerful infrastructure by insisting on the monotheistic worship of Aton as the one god.<br /><br />Highly recommended as a well-researched, immersive, and vibrant work of historical fiction. <br /><br />My reviews are also available at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.tamaraaghajaffar.com">www.tamaraaghajaffar.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4586468342870572764" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_990546673" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/990546673" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/990546673?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/25478735-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781556524417" href="/book/show/59282.The_Egyptian">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25478735-amanda?shelf=ancient-historical-fiction">ancient-historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer990546673" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15535915015141154692">Absolutely amazing. The most vivid and memorable book I can recall reading in recent memory. My favorite portrayal of Akhenaten, and one of the best depictions of ancient Egypt I've had the pleasure of digesting.<br/><br/>The only issue I had with it was that it did occasionally drag in parts, and there were some overlong descriptions of, for instance, how Sinuhe earned his wealth through the power of real estate, but overall this was just... wow. 10/10, would recommend.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_193422976" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/193422976" />
    <a title="Jody Mena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5943684-jody-mena"><img alt="Jody Mena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312304613p2/5943684.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/193422976?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jody Mena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jody Mena" href="/user/show/5943684-jody-mena">Jody Mena</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781556524417" href="/book/show/59282.The_Egyptian">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5943684-jody-mena?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer193422976" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14031971428282768705">A most remarkable tale of the dangers of fanaticism, the comfort of the familiar suffering, the superiority of wanting to having, the pitfalls of pride and the often hideous reality of human nature - the basest aspects of which we are so eager to ignore, thereby allowing to grow greater that the noble, which we fixate on desperately in order to assuage our collective shame as we keep our heads purposefully buried in the sand. This is a magnificent fable, and I believe its moral, if it were to ha</span>
  <span id="freeText14031971428282768705" style="display:none">A most remarkable tale of the dangers of fanaticism, the comfort of the familiar suffering, the superiority of wanting to having, the pitfalls of pride and the often hideous reality of human nature - the basest aspects of which we are so eager to ignore, thereby allowing to grow greater that the noble, which we fixate on desperately in order to assuage our collective shame as we keep our heads purposefully buried in the sand. This is a magnificent fable, and I believe its moral, if it were to have just one, would be "The road to hell is paved at every step with the best of intentions." Or perhaps "No man knows what tomorrow will bring" or "All was written in the stars before the day of my birth." Sinuhe certainly thought so. The irony in the fact that Sinuhe, the true heir to the throne, was the only one that did not try to take it by force while all manner of userpers believed they had the right to be Pharoh, and that he ended up miserable for the fact that he tried to do good and spread justice, is perfectly poetic as it holds a mirror up to the human condition. I do adore irony, and I love honesty, which this book held in full measure, I think. I have never read another book quite like this one. It may well become my favorite, and anyone who knows me will know that that is saying something.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14031971428282768705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_641344874" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/641344874" />
    <a title="Sanni" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18712477-sanni"><img alt="Sanni" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389007202p2/18712477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/641344874?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sanni" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sanni" href="/user/show/18712477-sanni">Sanni</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/131080.Sinuhe_egyptil_inen">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18712477-sanni?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer641344874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14452292928332368765">So I had to read this book for my Finnish class. I wasn't too excited about it because the book was always described to be "a Finnish classic", and, at least in my opinion, that is a synonym for boring. On top of that, this book had so many pages it almost made the Oxford dictionary look like a children's picture book.<br/><br/>However, when I started the book, I noticed I had never been so wrong. This book wasn't boring at all, in fact, it was quite the opposite. Within its hundreds of pages, the book he</span>
  <span id="freeText14452292928332368765" style="display:none">So I had to read this book for my Finnish class. I wasn't too excited about it because the book was always described to be "a Finnish classic", and, at least in my opinion, that is a synonym for boring. On top of that, this book had so many pages it almost made the Oxford dictionary look like a children's picture book.<br /><br />However, when I started the book, I noticed I had never been so wrong. This book wasn't boring at all, in fact, it was quite the opposite. Within its hundreds of pages, the book held everything one could possibly ask from a book. It was exciting, it was funny and it was sad. The book gave me action, romance, adventure, history and political schemes.<br /><br />This book tells the lifestory of a physician from ancient Egypt, from his early childhood to the very end of his life. The Egyptian, Sinuhe, always tries to do the right thing but no matter what he does, misfortune seems to follow him. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[A courtesan lures all of his fortune from him, he fails to save the love of his life from certain death, he is betrayed by his friend, and more. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />So I say: Do not fear the massiveness of the book, for it is worth all of your time. It was without a doubt the greatest book I have ever read, and it might be the greatest book I will ever read. Mika Waltari has restored my faith in Finnish literature.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14452292928332368765" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_461745238" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/461745238" />
    <a title="Galen Watson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10101553-galen-watson"><img alt="Galen Watson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442648360p2/10101553.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/461745238?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Galen Watson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Galen Watson" href="/user/show/10101553-galen-watson">Galen Watson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781556524417" href="/book/show/59282.The_Egyptian">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer461745238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11792809869681742651">The Egyptian is one of the finest Egyptian historical fictions ever written. At the same time, the author, Mika Waltari, crafted an adventure novel filled with philosophical overtones that leaves the reader pondering the meaning of life. And that’s what the book is about: an Egyptian’s entire life, lived during an era of historic and religious upheaval.<br/><br/>Sinuhe, the protagonist, puts idealism above all else, to the destruction of everything he loves. At the same time, he has a huge character flaw:</span>
  <span id="freeText11792809869681742651" style="display:none">The Egyptian is one of the finest Egyptian historical fictions ever written. At the same time, the author, Mika Waltari, crafted an adventure novel filled with philosophical overtones that leaves the reader pondering the meaning of life. And that’s what the book is about: an Egyptian’s entire life, lived during an era of historic and religious upheaval.<br /><br />Sinuhe, the protagonist, puts idealism above all else, to the destruction of everything he loves. At the same time, he has a huge character flaw: love for a woman he idealizes, who turns out to be nothing he imagined. Sinuhe is heroic, cowardly, self-interested, and idealistic—all wrapped up in one person. But he’s a transformational character and realizes at the end of his life that the problem with the world is people like himself.<br /><br />Finnish Author, Mika Waltari, created a masterpiece with this page-turner that will leave the reader wondering what is the value of ones beliefs?<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11792809869681742651" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_413787591" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/413787591" />
    <a title="Ryan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6857911-ryan"><img alt="Ryan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451250031p2/6857911.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/413787591?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ryan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ryan" href="/user/show/6857911-ryan">Ryan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio Download " href="/book/show/6239257-the-egyptian">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6857911-ryan?shelf=fic-historical">fic-historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer413787591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7237636496389475961">In The Egyptian (English translation), Mika Waltari takes us back to one of the oldest civilizations to tell one of the most classic stories there is: a young man rises from humble beginnings, makes a foolhardy choice, then is impelled to go out in the world and seek his fortune. He travels to other lands, learns about other customs, experiences different sides of life, and rises in stature by smartly applying his knowledge. Then he returns home again, where old friends and enemies await him.<br/><br/>I v</span>
  <span id="freeText7237636496389475961" style="display:none">In The Egyptian (English translation), Mika Waltari takes us back to one of the oldest civilizations to tell one of the most classic stories there is: a young man rises from humble beginnings, makes a foolhardy choice, then is impelled to go out in the world and seek his fortune. He travels to other lands, learns about other customs, experiences different sides of life, and rises in stature by smartly applying his knowledge. Then he returns home again, where old friends and enemies await him.<br /><br />I very much enjoyed The Egyptian's vibrant, convincing portrayal of ancient people's daily lives, superstitions, and familiar human flaws. Its timeless observations of how human societies operate still feel fresh. Rarely in Sinuhe's world is someone not exploiting, victimizing, or swindling someone else. When countries aren't terrorizing or fleecing their neighbors, they're wallowing in decadence, mired in poverty, or caught up in religious zeal. Who knows how historically accurate the depictions of the Syrians, Babylonians, Hittites, Cretans, and others are, but I liked the insights into different cultural personalities. It’s not hard to make connections to the unrest of Waltari’s own time.<br /><br />The story is somewhat less compelling, at least in Volume 1. Sinuhe goes from place to place as a physician, heals people, learns about the local culture and politics, then moves on. There are only a few characters that stick around long to become interesting. The one I enjoyed the most was Sinuhe's groveling, self-aggrandizing servant, Kaptah, whose personal badge of honor is that he doesn't steal more than a reasonable amount from his master (rendered in a delightfully Monty Python-esque voice in the audiobook). For a book from 1945, it's surprisingly full of sex, which Sinuhe seems to procure for himself everywhere he goes (apparently the author had his own Bohemian days). That said, Waltari's portrayal of women is a bit crude, with their role as sex objects being their main feature in the protagonist's eyes.<br /><br />Unfortunately, Volume 1 ends pretty abruptly, with a lot of unanswered questions left for Volume 2. The war and political chaos that Sinuhe is to witness has yet to unfold, though the region is teetering on the brink. I listened to the audiobook, which I got a few years ago, but seems to be out of “print” now. The narrator reads in an old school British theatre voice that suits the vaguely Biblical style of the prose well, though the recording isn’t the best -- you can hear the saliva smacking in his mouth as he talks (which goes awkwardly with the sexy moments).</span>
  <a data-text-id="7237636496389475961" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/435916530?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jani" href="/user/show/5905934-jani">Jani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789510207673" href="/book/show/197632.Sinuhe_egyptil_inen">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer435916530" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9677240651771677692">Longish classics are somewhat problematic: you'll be happy to buy them (especially if they are beautiful editions such as this), but they often end up spending years without reading just sitting on your shelf glaring at you disapprovingly with other accumulated peers (at least that's what it feels like to me). When you finally gather the willpower to start reading them (it is after all much easier to start a 300 page book than, say, 779 page one), there is always the possibility that you find th</span>
  <span id="freeText9677240651771677692" style="display:none">Longish classics are somewhat problematic: you'll be happy to buy them (especially if they are beautiful editions such as this), but they often end up spending years without reading just sitting on your shelf glaring at you disapprovingly with other accumulated peers (at least that's what it feels like to me). When you finally gather the willpower to start reading them (it is after all much easier to start a 300 page book than, say, 779 page one), there is always the possibility that you find the book's classic status much overrated (perhaps more based on its importance during its historical publication than its literary merits).<br /><br />Anyways, thank goodness Sinuhe lived up to its reputation. That is, it was an enjoyable historical novel that was certainly very readable and sometimes even a bit deep in its humanism. Its historical setting was also helped by the feeling of deep personal attachment by the author which was apparent, even without the scrap of knowledge that the novel was written much in a way to exorcise some of the personal demons caused by the WWII. This knowledge did somewhat affect my reading as a whole and once it was in my head it remained with me through the novel. I couldn't help but see the parallels with (especially the Finnish) experience of "the Second Great War" and was a bit reoccupied with wondering how the events of the ancient river Kingdoms and their neighbouring areas were connected with the events of the recent century. Perhaps, this preoccupation was a bit enhanced by some other books I have read during this years, which only goes to show the intertextuality of the reading experience; how you are always reading in a context of both the world, but the literary world as well.<br /><br />Anyways, I did enjoy the book in all its length, somewhat sigh-inducing humour and its slight repetitiveness. It had a heart: a heart that laughed, enjoyed life and almost as a consequence often bled. One could almost feel the distress of a writer torn with disbelief of the humanity he so much loved, at the same time celebrating its flaws as crying over its deep dark recesses that so blatantly had risen in the period before its publication to the fore of the human experience. There is ever darkness waiting for its turn in the human hearts and souls, but there is always hope for better to hold a torch against it advances. Perhaps, that wasn't what mr Waltari wanted to say, but that was what I got, and that is what matters.<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="9677240651771677692" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer321400380" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9384698733235480673">I have to say, I was apprehensive when I approached this book. I knew nothing about it in advance except that it's supposed to be some kind of literary classic written in the 1940s. I expected it to be ponderous, boring, high-minded and stuffy. But, book in hand, I thought "why not", took a deep breath, gritted my teeth and dove in. <br/><br/>To my surprise I found that this book is anything but boring and stuffy. It is, above all, an entertaining and very human tale that makes ancient Egypt feel like a r</span>
  <span id="freeText9384698733235480673" style="display:none">I have to say, I was apprehensive when I approached this book. I knew nothing about it in advance except that it's supposed to be some kind of literary classic written in the 1940s. I expected it to be ponderous, boring, high-minded and stuffy. But, book in hand, I thought "why not", took a deep breath, gritted my teeth and dove in. <br /><br />To my surprise I found that this book is anything but boring and stuffy. It is, above all, an entertaining and very human tale that makes ancient Egypt feel like a real place with real people. The characters are all colorfully drawn with a lighthearted, ironic eye, and the book just whooshes by despite it's length. <br /><br />If you can get your hands on Waltari's other books, The Adventurer and The Wanderer, I recommend them as well, as they share the same qualities the make The Egyptian great.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2674461187" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14737630177418255450">Wow, what a journey!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_3490639892" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3490639892" />
    <a title="Vera" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/111258113-vera"><img alt="Vera" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583963642p2/111258113.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3490639892?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vera" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vera" href="/user/show/111258113-vera">Vera</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/131080.Sinuhe_egyptil_inen">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/111258113-vera?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3490639892" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2366207913927630336">Easily the most tiresome book I've read. The best book I didn't like, if that makes any sense at all. The story itself was thrilling at its best and I mean we love ancient Egypt as the setting. At times Waltari was really able to paint a picture with his words. Loved the theme of the characters falling in and out of fortune: that was the main thing that made me keep on reading. But MY GOD was it a task - I can't remember the last time I've had to put this much conscious effort into finishing a b</span>
  <span id="freeText2366207913927630336" style="display:none">Easily the most tiresome book I've read. The best book I didn't like, if that makes any sense at all. The story itself was thrilling at its best and I mean we love ancient Egypt as the setting. At times Waltari was really able to paint a picture with his words. Loved the theme of the characters falling in and out of fortune: that was the main thing that made me keep on reading. But MY GOD was it a task - I can't remember the last time I've had to put this much conscious effort into finishing a book. As in, I mean no disrespect to marathon runners but I think it's by far the bigger feat to make it to the end of this godforsaken novel. <br /><br />At first I enjoyed Sinuhe's rambling and attentive narration, but by the second part it mostly just felt unnecessary and made me want to set the book on fire. All sentences were the same length and constructed in the same way so there was no rhythm to the text. Every now and then I actually had to resort to speed reading or skipping paragraphs but I'll defend myself by saying that had I not done it my brain might have rotted and I still need it for other things.<br /><br />Also tedious was the racist language that was so frequent I was afraid my eyes would never return to their usual place from how much I was rolling them (yes it's a product of it's time yadda yadda but that's not an excuse to not judge it hard). There is not a single reason why ancient Egyptians would have used racist expressions of the modern era in 14th century BCE ?? With all the immense authority that being a history student gives me I just wanna say that that's anachronistic and literally so annoying. <br /><br />And then. *deep inhale* I don't know when male authors learned that there are other ways to describe women than 'old and ugly' and 'young and hot', or alternatively by the look of their tits, but it was definitely after Waltari wrote Sinuhe. Apparently he couldn't write a convincing woman character if his life depended on it (let me summarise: 'Women are dangerous but like, so sexy ;)') If a woman character is introduced and you're worried that you won't know what their boobs look like, do not fret! You can be sure that a sentence like "her breasts are hanging like dry leather bags" or "her rosy breast was indeed very lush and well worth a look" soon follows. My personal fave was when a man is executed and his dying wish is that her wife expose her "blossoming breasts" one last time. So moving you could cry innit. I wish I had collected all the boob-related brain farts so that whenever I'm feeling down about not being eloquent enough in the great literary work that is my journal, I could look at them and realise I've got nothing to worry about. Again, product of it's time, but how the fuck am I supposed to take seriously a book that could be renamed '101 Creepy Ass Ways to Talk About Tits'?<br /><br />I'm kind of disappointed that I didn't love it because in theory it looks right up my alley. Basically it was a contrary and just plain weird reading experience: the good parts were good enough to make me desperate to know what happens next but more often than not I just wanted every new page to be the last. Honestly, anyone who's made it to the end of this book is braver than the US marines and if it were any other book I wouldn't have bothered, but I'm a Finn and thus persevered and I guess I'm a better, more educated citizen with a more refined sense of our national achievements now that I've read one of our great classics. Idk man I'm just glad it's over.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2366207913927630336" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_239535320" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/239535320" />
    <a title="Clark Hays" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6829322-clark-hays"><img alt="Clark Hays" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1335846660p2/6829322.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/239535320?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clark Hays" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clark Hays" href="/user/show/6829322-clark-hays">Clark Hays</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781556524417" href="/book/show/59282.The_Egyptian">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer239535320" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2643175211504884436"><b>“To each day its own vexations”</b><br/><br/><i>The Egyptian</i> is a classic in the truest sense and an epic (not a word I use lightly) tale resonating with truth, power and poignant insights into the human condition that bridge the centuries. <br/><br/>It was written by Mika Waltari who, according to the back of the book, is widely considered the greatest Finnish writer of the 20th century. Regardless of his provenance, he is simply a great writer. That <i>The Egyptian</i> was sent as a gift by a Finnish friend and book blogger (t</span>
  <span id="freeText2643175211504884436" style="display:none"><b>“To each day its own vexations”</b><br /><br /><i>The Egyptian</i> is a classic in the truest sense and an epic (not a word I use lightly) tale resonating with truth, power and poignant insights into the human condition that bridge the centuries. <br /><br />It was written by Mika Waltari who, according to the back of the book, is widely considered the greatest Finnish writer of the 20th century. Regardless of his provenance, he is simply a great writer. That <i>The Egyptian</i> was sent as a gift by a Finnish friend and book blogger (thanks Niina at, shameless plug, For the Love of Reading) made it all the more intriguing. <br /><br />The book chronicles the life of Sinuhe, the lonely one and son of the wild ass, an orphan who becomes physician to the pharaohs and serves as a witness, and architect, of momentous events in Egyptian history. His life, travails and loves intersect with key political events and battles that shape the future of Egypt, including the origins of King Tut. <br /><br />According to the back of the book, <i>The Egyptian</i> was condemned as obscene when published in the U.S. in 1949. There are many veiled references to sharing mats with women or grasping the loins of lovers, etc., and one particularly cruel scene involving a royal and monumental cuckolding, but it’s not the sex or the empowered women (possibly more so than capable within their era), that made the book obscene. In 1949 America, it was dangerous. <br /><br />Sinhue has a slow awakening across the decades – thanks to his roaming throughout the various lands and his proximity to the leaders – that all religions are false and all governments are equally ineffective and powered only by greed and the petty desires and shortcomings of those in power. “No nation is either braver or more chickenhearted, crueler or more compassionate, wickeder or more virtuous than another.” That notion would not have set well with American exceptionalism, especially as McCarthyism was festering to fruition. <br /><br />It’s probably dangerous by today’s standards as well. As religions clashed and priests and lords scrambled to control power, the poor were caught in the middle. I saw much of the politics of the present day reflected in the careful description so that ancient Egypt seemed alive and well and all around us. <br /><br />I always worry about translations, and how much of the original lyricism and power is lost, but in this case, in which a Finnish writer endeavored to capture an Egyptian style, it seemed to work well with much rending of garments, oiling of heads and gnashing of teeth. I also wonder about the accuracy of the portrayal of life in ancient times because, as a work of fiction, there are no discussions of research or source material. I do know this: After reading <i>The Egyptian</i>, I will always think of it when I imagine life in 14th century B.C.E. That’s a powerful book. <br /><br />I highly recommend it and suggest adding it to your “to read” list because “Our time is short, and no one knows what tomorrow may bring…"</span>
  <a data-text-id="2643175211504884436" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_339683805" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/339683805" />
    <a title="Mandy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/874587-mandy"><img alt="Mandy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1549324724p2/874587.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/339683805?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mandy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mandy" href="/user/show/874587-mandy">Mandy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789510119891" href="/book/show/10768630-the-egyptian">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/874587-mandy?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/874587-mandy?shelf=historical">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer339683805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8444549639969689262">What a sad yet wonderful tale. Written in first person point of view as the life story of a man who lived in ancient Egypt during the time of the later pharoahs, it has a reflective and melancholy tone. I think perhaps I enjoyed it so much because it incorporates several historical figures that are part of Egyptian history and I knew something of this history before I began reading this book. I suspect that is part of what drew me to it in the first place. The story is fascinating in its way, an</span>
  <span id="freeText8444549639969689262" style="display:none">What a sad yet wonderful tale. Written in first person point of view as the life story of a man who lived in ancient Egypt during the time of the later pharoahs, it has a reflective and melancholy tone. I think perhaps I enjoyed it so much because it incorporates several historical figures that are part of Egyptian history and I knew something of this history before I began reading this book. I suspect that is part of what drew me to it in the first place. The story is fascinating in its way, and has all the elements that make for a good story (war, intrigue, love, loss, and so on).<br /><br />I don't know whether other people would enjoy this as much as I did. Other people I know who tried to read it found it slow moving and uninteresting. I found it fun and informative even though the main character is often maudlin in his recollections. There is much in the writing and tone that contributes to the idea that the main character is a learned and contemplative man, and that contributes much to the story and the accounts made of the other characters. I think the guy who wrote it must have been pretty well versed in the supposed culture of ancient Egypt, as cultural aspects and attitudes of the period figure heavily in characters' actions.<br /><br />If you're into semi-historical fiction that involves spinning a yarn around historic events and the prominent figures therein, then this is a book for you. If not, you most likely won't take as much pleasure from it as I did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8444549639969689262" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_246198349" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/246198349" />
    <a title="Brahadeesh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6358678-brahadeesh"><img alt="Brahadeesh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328574850p2/6358678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/246198349?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brahadeesh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brahadeesh" href="/user/show/6358678-brahadeesh">Brahadeesh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781556524417" href="/book/show/59282.The_Egyptian">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer246198349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15801420294420342711">One of the best historic novels I have read so far. Simple yet profound illustration of the religious and political conflicts during the Pharoah Akhenaton's reign, founder of one of the earliest monotheistic religion. The story revolves around the travels and expeditions of a Egyptian physician named Sinuhe and the socio-political scenario of the countries he visits during his life. The journey of this physician is so eventful with cruelty of humans, fragility and wickedness of human mind, love </span>
  <span id="freeText15801420294420342711" style="display:none">One of the best historic novels I have read so far. Simple yet profound illustration of the religious and political conflicts during the Pharoah Akhenaton's reign, founder of one of the earliest monotheistic religion. The story revolves around the travels and expeditions of a Egyptian physician named Sinuhe and the socio-political scenario of the countries he visits during his life. The journey of this physician is so eventful with cruelty of humans, fragility and wickedness of human mind, love etc. <br /><br />Beside the lively illustration of the socio-political scenario of Egypt and Syria 3500 years ago, there is a touch of pessimism although I personally liked it. And there are some discrepancies in some historical facts. As far as I know Horemheb was childless but he is begets a child according to this novel.<br /><br />I guess there are some issues with the translation from Finnish to English, many times the author speaks about corn cultivation and corn reserves etc. Corn was never grown in Egypt, at least I know that much for sure. <br /><br />Casting one or two translation errors away and little twist in historical fact, I would say the book is well written and is a best bet for people who would like to read historical novels during their leisure time. I read the translated version of 'The Egyptian' by Naomi Walford.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="15801420294420342711" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
